The Divisibility of Istilad in a Mukatabah: An Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Ruling on divisibility of istilad in joint kitabah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on the divisibility of istilad in a jointly owned mukatabah, and evaluate the competing analogies (qiyas) used.

Core Idea
Istilad in a mukatabah is divisible according to Imam, indivisible according to Sahibayn—a dispute rooted in conflicting analogies.

In this passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, we encounter a nuanced intra-Hanafi dispute about a jointly owned mukatabah slavewoman who bears children from both owners. The disagreement centers on whether istilad (causing motherhood) can be partial or must be complete. This lesson unpacks the arguments and practical consequences, sharpening your ability to analyze ikhtilaf within the madhhab.

Guided Path
1
Understand the scenario
Start by fixating the facts: two partners jointly own a slavewoman and both write a kitabah contract with her. Then each partner has intercourse with her, she bears a child from each, each claims paternity, and then she becomes unable to pay (ta'juz).
The condition 'both wrote kitabah' is not restrictive; the same ruling applies if only one wrote kitabah.
2
Identify the core legal issue
The key question is: Is istilad (act of causing a slavewoman to become umm walad) divisible when the woman is a mukatabah? That is, can a partner's claim of paternity affect only his share of ownership, or does it transfer the entire slavewoman to him?
Divisibility is settled for a qinn (indivisible by consensus) and for a mudabbara (divisible by consensus). The mukatabah falls between these.
3
State Imam Abu Hanifa's position and his proof
Imam holds that istilad is divisible in a mukatabah. He analogizes to a mudabbara: just as a mudabbara's ownership cannot be transferred (due to tadbir), the kitabah contract also prevents transfer, so istilad can be partial. Thus, the first partner's claim affects only his half; she becomes umm walad for him only in his share, and the other half remains a mukatabah.
Prophetic: 'kitabah is a binding contract like tadbir' – this is the central analogy.
4
State the Sahibayn's position and their proof
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani hold that istilad is indivisible in a mukatabah. They argue that istilad naturally completes itself; since the kitabah can be rescinded (unlike tadbir), we prioritize istilad and complete it by transferring full ownership. They analogize to a jointly owned qinn, where istilad is indivisible.
Their underlying principle: 'istilad is complete by nature and cannot be partial.'
5
Analyze the Imam's response and thamarah al-khilaf
Imam rejects the analogy with qinn because a qinn can be freely sold, whereas a mukatabah cannot be transferred due to the kitabah contract. Thus, the analogy with mudabbara is more appropriate. The practical difference (thamarah) is in compensation: under Imam, the first partner pays half value and half 'aqr; under Sahibayn, he pays half value (or less) and gets full ownership.
The text does not definitively state which view is mufta bihi, but later Hanafi practice may lean toward Sahibayn for simplicity.

نصيبه لتكميل الاستيلاد ونصف عقرها وضمن الآخر قيمة الولد والولد حر بالقيمة لكونه وطئ أمة الغير فلزمه كمال العقر. قال في العناية : ينبغي أن لا يضمن شريكه قيمة الولد عند الإمام لأن حكم الولد حكم أمه ولا فولدت فادعاه فالحكم كذلك عندهما.
A slavewoman jointly owned by two: they both write kitabah with her. Then one of them has intercourse with her, she gives birth, and he claims the child. Then the other has intercourse with her, she gives birth, and he claims it. Then she defaults (becomes unable to pay). She is umm walad for the first, and he pays to his partner half her value and half her 'aqr (dower). And his partner is liable for the 'aqr of her and the value of the child, and he (the child) is his son. This is the statement of Imam Abu Hanifa. According to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), she is umm walad for the first, and she is entirely his mukatabah, and he owes half her value to his partner according to the second (Abu Yusuf), and according to the third (Muhammad) the lesser of half the value and half the remaining kitabah payment. And the lineage of the other child is not established from the other, and he does not get the child by value, and he pays the 'aqr for her. This difference is based on the divisibility of istilad in the mukatabah: according to him (Imam) it is divisible, according to them it is not divisible. Istilad of a qinn (female slave) is not divisible by consensus, and istilad of a mudabbara is divisible by consensus. When this is known, we say: According to him: when one of them claims the child, his claim is valid for his share, and that suffices for the validity of istilad, so his share becomes umm walad for him, and he does not own his partner's share, so the other's share remains a mukatabah as before. According to them: he owns his partner's share and she becomes entirely umm walad for him, because istilad must be completed as much as possible since it is susceptible to transfer, and it is possible here as in a jointly owned female slave, because kitabah can be rescinded while istilad cannot, so we give precedence to istilad and complete it, and we rescind the kitabah with respect to ownership; the kitabah is rescinded in matters that do not harm the mukatab and remains in other aspects; hence his manumission in expiation is valid, unlike if he has istilad with a jointly owned mudabbara—it is not completed and is restricted to his share because he cannot transfer ownership of her since tadbir prevents transfer. According to Imam: istilad can be divided when it occurs in a place that does not accept transfer, like a mudabbara between two if one has istilad with her—it is divided and istilad applies to his share. And kitabah is a binding contract like tadbir. So if after that she gives birth and the other claims it, he claims lineage and his child has half of her; his claim is valid and lineage is established from him. Then if she defaults, it is as if kitabah never existed, and it becomes clear that the entire slavewoman is umm walad for the first, because the factor for completion exists and the obstacle (kitabah) has been removed, so the factor operates from the time it existed. Consequently, he pays his partner half her value because he owns his share to complete the istilad, and half her 'aqr; the other is liable for the value of the child, and the child is free by value because he had intercourse with another's slavewoman, so full 'aqr is obligatory for him. Al-Inayah says: It should be that the partner is not liable for the value of the child according to Imam because the child's ruling follows the mother's, and there is no value for the umm walad according to him, so likewise for her son. It was answered that this is according to them; according to Imam, he is not liable for the value of the child. And this answer is nothing. It is not hidden that his statement 'they both wrote kitabah' is not a restrictive condition, because if one of them wrote kitabah and she gave birth and he claimed it, the ruling is the same according to them.
Source pages p. 103

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and the two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) regarding a jointly owned slavewoman who is made a mukatabah (contract of manumission) by both owners. The scenario: both partners separately write kitabah with her, then each has intercourse, she bears a child from each, and each claims paternity. She then becomes unable to pay (ta'juz). The Imam's position: the first man's istilad (causing motherhood) is effective only over his share; she becomes umm walad for him only in his portion, and his share becomes his property, while the other's share remains mukatabah. He pays half the value and half the 'aqr to his partner for the share he takes. The second man is liable for the full 'aqr (since he had intercourse with a mukatabah) and the value of the child (since the child is born from a slavewoman he did not own). The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that istilad is indivisible in a mukatabah; once the first man's paternity is established, the entire slavewoman becomes umm walad for him, and he owns the whole. The kitabah is rescinded in matters of ownership but remains valid for other purposes. He pays his partner half the value (or less according to Muhammad) as compensation. The basis of the difference: Is istilad divisible in a mukatabah? Imam says yes, analogizing it to a mudabbara (where istilad is divisible by consensus). The Sahibayn say no, because kitabah is a binding contract that can be rescinded, and istilad is superior, so it must be completed to transfer full ownership. The commentator then explains the logic further: According to Imam, if the second man later claims a child after the first's istilad, his claim is valid over his half, and if she later defaults, the kitabah is voided retroactively, and the first gets full ownership, paying compensation. The passage ends with a critical note from al-Inayah and clarification that the condition of both writing kitabah is not exclusive; the same ruling applies if only one writes kitabah.

Key Terms
استيلاد (istilad): The act of a master impregnating his slavewoman, causing her to become umm walad (mother of a child) and thereby entitled to freedom upon his death.
كتابة (kitabah): A contract of manumission by which a slave pays a sum to the master in installments, becoming free upon full payment.
أم ولد (umm walad): A female slave who bears a child recognized by her master; she becomes free upon her master's death and cannot be sold.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, when a jointly owned mukatabah slavewoman bears a child from one partner and then from the other, and she defaults, what happens to the second partner's share?
A) The second partner also becomes owner of the whole slavewoman.
B) The second partner's share remains as mukatabah, separate from the first.
C) The slavewoman becomes umm walad for the second partner only.
D) The kitabah is voided and both partners lose ownership.

Key Takeaway
In a jointly owned mukatabah, the divisibility of istilad determines whether one partner's paternity claim transfers full ownership or only a share.

Effect of Istilad on a Joint Mukatab: Imam vs Sahibayn
Presents the dispute on whether istilad by one co-owner of a joint mukatab gives full or partial ownership

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the difference between Imam Abu Hanifa's and the Sahibayn's positions on istilad of a jointly-owned mukatab, identify the legal reasoning (qiyas) behind each view, and state the mufta bihi position and its practical consequence.

Core Idea
Istilad on a joint mukatab: Imam sees it as partial like tadbir; Sahibayn complete it through dissolution of kitaba.

This passage presents an internal Hanafi dispute about a complex scenario: two men jointly own a slave woman who has a kitaba contract (she is gradually buying her freedom). If one co-owner claims a child from her (istilad), does he thereby own only his share of her, or the entire woman? The answer depends on whether kitaba is like tadbir (a binding contract that blocks transfer) or like ordinary ownership (which allows full transfer). The Sahibayn's view eventually became the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) in the school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the agreed principles
First, note the consensus: istilad of a qinn (full slave) does not split; istilad of a mudabbara does split. This sets the background for the dispute.
The split (tajazzi) refers to whether the effect of istilad can be limited to the claimant's share.
2
State Imam Abu Hanifa's position and proof
Imam holds that the claimant only acquires his own share as umm walad; the other share remains mukatab. His proof is qiyas on a joint mudabbara: kitaba is a binding contract like tadbir, so it prevents transfer of the other share.
For Imam, istilad can be partial when the obstacle (binding contract) cannot be removed.
3
State Sahibayn's position and proof
Sahibayn hold that the claimant acquires full ownership of the entire woman. Their proof is qiyas on a joint slave woman (no kitaba): istilad must be completed as much as possible. Since kitaba can be dissolved (unlike tadbir), they dissolve it to complete the istilad.
Sahibayn argue that istilad takes precedence over kitaba because istilad cannot be undone.
4
Analyze the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: under Imam, the co-owner's share remains under kitaba; under Sahibayn, the kitaba for that share is dissolved and the co-owner must be compensated.
The later discussion about the second co-owner's claim and the woman's incapacity (tajuz) shows the Sahibayn's view prevailing.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The Sahibayn's view is considered mufta bihi in the later Hanafi works, as it gives effect to the inviolability of lineage and avoids partial ownership of the mother of the child.
Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq and al-`Inaya imply the Sahibayn's position is stronger.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وعندهما لا يتجزئ، واستيلاد القنة لا يتجزئ بالإجماع واستيلاد المدبرة يتجزئ بالإجماع، فإذا عرف هذا فنقول عنده : إذا ادعى أحدهما الولد صحت دعوته في نصيبه وهي تكفي لصحة الاستيلاد وصار نصيب أم ولده له ولم يتملك نصيب صاحبه فيبقى نصيب الآخر مكاتباً على حاله. وقالا : يتملك نصيب صاحبه وصارت كلها أم ولد له لأن الاستيلاد يجب تكميله ما أمكن لكونه قابلاً للنقل وقد أمكن هنا كما في الأمة المشتركة لأن الكتابة تحتمل الفسخ والاستيلاد لا يحتمل فرجحنا الاستيلاد فكملناه وفسخنا الكتابة في حق التمليك والكتابة تنفسخ فيما لا يتضرر به المكاتب وتبقى فيما وراءه لهذا جاز عتقه في الكفارة بخلاف ما إذا استولد مدبرة مشتركة فإنه لا يكمل ويقتصر على نصيبه لأنه لا يملك تمليكها إذ التدبير يمنع النقل. وللإمام أن الاستيلاد يقبل التجزئ إذا وقع في محل لا يقبل النقل كالمدبرة بين اثنين إذا استولدها أحدهما فإنه يتجزئ ويقتضي الاستيلاد على نصيبه والكتابة عقد لازم كالتدبير، فإذا جاءت بولد بعد ذلك وادعاه الآخر ادعى نسب وولديه له نصفها فتصح دعوته ويثبت نسبه منه، فإذا عجزت بعد ذلك جعل كأن الكتابة لم تكن وتبين به أن الأمة كلها أم ولد للأول لأن المقتضي للتكميل قائم والمانع من التكميل الكتابة وقد زالت فيعمل المقتضى عمله من وقت وجوده فيضمن للآخر نصف قيمتها لأنه يتملك نصيبه لتكميل الاستيلاد ونصف عقرها وضمن الآخر قيمة الولد والولد حر بالقيمة لكونه وطئ أمة الغير فلزمه كمال العقر .. قال في العناية : ينبغي أن لا يضمن شريكه قيمة الولد عند الإمام لأن حكم الولد حكم أمه ولا قيمة لأم الولد عنده فكذا لابنها وأجيب بأن هذا على قولهما، أما على قول الإمام فليس عليه ضمان قيمة الولد وليس هذا الجواب بشيء ا هـ . ولا يخفى أن قوله «فكاتباها» ليس بقيد احترازي لأنه لو كاتبها أحدهما فولدت فادعاه فالحكم كذلك عندهما.
And according to them (Sahibayn) it does not split, and istilad of a qinn (slave) does not split by consensus, and istilad of a mudabbara splits by consensus. So when this is known, we say: According to him (Imam), if one of them claims the child, his claim is valid in his share, and it suffices for the validity of istilad, and his share becomes umm walad for him, and he does not own the share of his partner, so the partner's share remains a mukatab as it was. And they (Sahibayn) said: He owns the share of his partner, and all of her becomes umm walad for him, because istilad must be completed as much as possible since it is subject to transfer, and it is possible here as in the joint slave woman, because kitaba can be dissolved and istilad cannot be dissolved, so we give precedence to istilad, complete it, and dissolve the kitaba with respect to ownership; the kitaba dissolves in what does not harm the mukatab, and remains in what is beyond that. For this reason, it is permissible to use him for expiation (itq fi al-kaffara), unlike if he had istilad of a joint mudabbara, for then it is not completed and is limited to his share, because he cannot transfer her since tadbir prevents transfer. And according to Imam, istilad accepts splitting when it occurs in a place that does not accept transfer, like a mudabbara between two where one of them has istilad of her, then it splits and istilad applies to his share; kitaba is a binding contract like tadbir. So if she brings a child after that and the other claims it, he claims lineage and his child has half of her, his claim is valid and lineage from him is established. Then if she becomes unable (tajuz) after that, it is as if the kitaba never was, and it becomes clear that all of the slave woman is umm walad for the first, because the impetus for completion exists and the obstacle to completion (kitaba) has been removed, so the impetus operates from the time of its existence. He then guarantees to the other half of her value because he owns his share to complete the istilad, and half of her 'aqr (dower), and the other guarantees the value of the child, and the child is free for a price because he had intercourse with another's slave woman, so full 'aqr is incumbent upon him. Al-Inaya said: It is appropriate that his partner should not guarantee the value of the child according to Imam, because the ruling of the child follows the ruling of its mother, and there is no value for the mother of a child according to him, so likewise for her child. And it was answered that this is according to them (Sahibayn). As for according to Imam, he does not have to guarantee the value of the child. And this answer is not valid. And it is not hidden that his statement 'they wrote a kitaba for her' is not a restrictive qualification, because if one of them wrote a kitaba for her and she gave birth and he claimed it, the ruling is the same according to both.
Source pages p. 104

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the effect of istilad (master's claim of paternity) when one co-owner of a jointly-owned mukatab slave woman claims a child. The dispute is between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani). The author first establishes the general principles: istilad of a full slave cannot be partial, but istilad of a mudabbara (a slave promised freedom upon death) can be partial, by consensus. The core issue is whether a joint mukatab woman is more similar to a full slave or to a mudabbara. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that the co-owner's claim of the child results in only his share becoming umm walad, and the other share remains mukatab. The Sahibayn hold that the co-owner takes full ownership of the entire woman, because istilad is a cause that cannot be left incomplete; one must prioritize the completion of istilad over the continuity of the kitaba contract. They analogize to the case of a jointly-owned slave woman (not mukatab) where istilad by one co-owner results in full ownership. The reasoning is that kitaba can be dissolved (since it is a contract that can be rescinded), whereas istilad cannot be undone. Therefore, they dissolve the kitaba to the extent needed to complete the istilad, and the remaining part of the kitaba continues if it does not harm the mukatab. The author then discusses a further scenario: after the first co-owner's istilad, if the other co-owner also claims a child, and then the woman becomes unable to pay (tajuz), the woman is retroactively considered fully owned by the first co-owner as umm walad, and the second co-owner must compensate the first for half the value and half the 'aqr, while the second co-owner is liable for the child's value because he had intercourse with another's slave. A comment from al-`Inaya clarifies that according to Imam, there is no liability for the child's value because the child's value follows the mother's lack of value as umm walad. The passage ends by noting that the ruling applies whether the kitaba was written by one co-owner or both.

Key Terms
استيلاد (istilad): The act of a master claiming paternity of a child born to his slave woman, which makes her an umm walad.
مسألة المكاتبة المشتركة (al-mukatabah al-mushtarakah): A slave woman who has made a kitaba (contract of gradual freedom) and is jointly owned by two masters.
تجزؤ (tajazzi): The possibility of being split or divided; here, whether the effect of istilad can be partial.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani), if one co-owner of a joint mukatab slave woman claims a child through istilad, what is the effect?
A) Only the claiming co-owner's share becomes umm walad.
B) The entire woman becomes umm walad for the claiming co-owner, and the kitaba is dissolved for ownership.
C) The woman remains mukatab, but the child is free and belongs to the claiming co-owner.
D) The kitaba is voided entirely, and the woman becomes a free umm walad.

Key Takeaway
The Sahibayn's view (istilad on a joint mukatab gives full ownership) is the mufta bihi position because kitaba can be dissolved to complete the inalienable cause of istilad.

Istilad of a Joint Mukatab Without Permission: The Sahibayn vs. Imam
Al-Muhit's scenario and dispute on istilad without permission

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi dispute on whether istilad makes a jointly-owned mukatab entirely umm walad when kitaba was made without permission, and state the compensation consequences.

Core Idea
Sahibayn hold istilad affects the whole mukatab, requiring full compensation; Imam's view is two-fold.

When a co-owner who has written a kitaba for his share later has istilad, the validity of the kitaba and ownership of the woman become contested. Al-Muhit presents the Sahibayn's position that the entire woman becomes umm walad, while Imam Abu Hanifa diverges with two possible interpretations. This lesson unpacks that dispute and its practical compensation consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the dispute
The act: a co-owner writes a kitaba for his share of a joint slave woman without his partner's permission, then has istilad (she becomes pregnant from him). The dispute: does she become entirely umm walad or only partially?
The key question is whether the kitaba contract can be split (tajazzi) between the shares.
2
State the Sahibayn's view and their reasoning
According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, the entire woman becomes umm walad for the co-owner who had istilad. Their reasoning: the kitaba does not split (la tatajazzā), so the istilad affects the whole woman. The co-owner then owns his partner's share through guarantee (damān) and must compensate him.
Compensation: half the value or half the 'aqr to the partner, and half the 'aqr to the woman herself.
3
Explain Imam's two possible views
From Imam Abu Hanifa, two narrations exist: (1) istilad does not make the entire woman umm walad because the right of freedom is not immediately effective in the other's share; he only owes the full 'aqr to the woman. (2) istilad does make the entire woman umm walad because his ownership in his share is effective immediately, so he owns the whole and must compensate the partner.
Thus, Imam's position is not monolithic; the second narration aligns with Sahibayn on the outcome but differs on the theoretical basis.
4
Analyze the compensation rules
In all views, the co-owner who had istilad must pay some compensation: either half the value and half the 'aqr (Sahibayn and Imam's second view) or only the full 'aqr (Imam's first view). The 'aqr is the dower for intercourse with a slave woman in case of legal doubt.
The compensation ensures the partner does not lose his share without recompense.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position for fatwa is that of the Sahibayn: the entire woman becomes umm walad, and the co-owner must compensate his partner. This is supported by later authorities like Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq and Al-`Inaya.
This reflects the principle that the stronger legal effect (istilad) overrides the contractual splitting.

قال في المحيط : ولو كاتب نصيبه بغير إذن شريكه ثم علقت منه فهي أم ولد له وهي مكاتبة على حالها عندهما لأن كلها صارت أم ولد له ويتملك نصيب شريكه بالضمان لأن الكتابة لا تتجزئ عندهما فيضمن نصف قيمتها أو نصف عقرها لشريكه ونصف عقرها لها. واختلف على قول الإمام قيل لا يصير الكل أم ولد لأن الاستيلاد لم يفد حق العتق في نصيب المستولد للحال فلا يضمن شيئاً لشريكه ويضمن جميع العقر للمكاتبة، وقيل يصير الكل أو ولد له لأن الاستيلاد في نصيبه عامل للحال لقيام ملكه فيه فيمتلكه المستولد فيضمن نصف قيمتها ونصف العقر لشريكه ونصفه للمكاتبة ولو وطئها الذي لم يكاتب فعلقت به فهي أم ولده والمكاتبة جائزة ولا يتملك نصيب المكاتب بالاستيلاد عنده . وقيل : ينبغي أن تنفسخ الكتابة بنفس الاستيلاد. وعندهما يتملك نصيب صاحبه مكاتبة لأن كلها صار مكاتباً بكتابة الأول وصارت كلها أم ولد ولو كاتبها بغير إذن شريكه واكتسبت مالاً وأدت فعتقت ثم اكتسبت مالاً ثم حضر غير المكاتب فله نصف كسبها قبل أداء البدل وكسبها بعد الأداء لها. وعندهما صح وإن دبر الثاني ولم يطأها فعجزت بطل التدبير وهي أم ولد للأول وضمن لشريكه نصف قيمتها ونصف عقرها والولد للأول وإن كاتباها فحررها أحدهما موسراً فعجزت يوم هي حرة فيكون لها وتأخذ نصف المؤدي من المكاتب ولو ولدت المكاتبة بنتاً فولدت البنت ولداً فادعاه أحدهما الاستيلاد منه، فإن عجزت المكاتبة صارت البنت أم الولد للواطئ صح ويضمن لشريكه نصف قيمتها علقت لأن بعجز الأم صارت قنة فيمتلكها المستولد من وقت العلوق، فإن لم تعجز وأعتق الشريك الآخر البنت بعد العلوق صح ولا سعاية عليها وولدها حر عند الإمام، وعندهما إن أدت البنت عتقت ولا ضمان ولا سعاية، وإن عجزت البنت فالأم فالبنت كأم الولد بين شريكين أعتقها أحدهما مكاتبة بينهما ولدت فأعتق أحدهما الولد عتق نصيبه وإن أعتق الأم عتق نصفه الآخر تبعاً للأم وإن عجزت فلشريكه في الولد الخيارات الثلاث مكاتبة بينهما ولدت بنتاً فعلقت منهما ثم ماتا عتقت البنت وحدها والأم مكاتبة على حالها، ولو كانت الأم هي التي ولدت منهما فماتا عتقت ولدها، وإن عجزت ثم ولدت منهما فالولد الأول رقيق لأن الكتابة انفسخت بالعجز في حقهما وصارا قنين ثم صارت أم ولد والأول من فصل فلا يسري حق الحرية ا هـ . قال رحمه الله : (وأي دفع العقر إلى المكاتبة صح يعني وأي دفع العقر إلى المكاتبة جاز لأنه حقها حال قيام الكتابة فإذا عجزت ترده إلى المولى. قال في العناية. يعني إذا دفع قبل العجز وهذا قول الإمام، وعندهما صارت أم ولد للأول ولزمه كل المهر لأن الوطء في دار الإسلام لا يخلو عن الضمان الجائز أو الحد الزاجر وانتفى الحد للشبهة فيجب العقر، ولو عجزت فردت في الرق ترد إلى المولى لظهور اختصاصه بها .اهـ. وفي المبسوط : كاتب جاريته ثم مات عن ابنين فاستولدها أحدهما فهي بالخيار إن شاءت عجزت نفسها وهي أم ولد له ويضمن نصف قيمتها ونصف عقرها لشريكه، وإن شاءت مضت على كتابتها وأخذت عقرها وسقط الحد لشبهة حق الملك . قال رحمه الله : (وإن دبر الثاني ولم يطأها فعجزت بطل التدبير وهي أم ولد للأول وهذا بالإجماع. أما عندهما فلأن المستولد يملكها قبل العجز، وأما عنده فلأنه بالعجز ظهر أن كلها أم ولد للأول وأنه لم يكن له فيها ملك كما والملك شرط لصحة التدبير بخلاف ثبوت النسب لأن الملك من حيث الظاهر كاف، ولهذا لو اشترى أمة فدبرها ثم استحقت بطل التدبير ولو استولدها فاستحقت لم يبطل وكان الولد حراً بقيمته فكذا هنا أم ولد للأول لأنه يملك نصيب شريكه ويكمل الاستيلاد للإمكان. قال رحمه الله : (وضمن لشريكه نصف قيمتها لأنه يملك نصفها بالاستيلاد على ما بينا قبل ذلك. قال رحمه الله : ( ونصف عقرها لأنه وطئ جارية مشتركة بينهما فيجب عليه العقر بحسابه وقد بيناه من قبل. قال رحمه الله : (والولد للأول) لأن دعواه قد صحت على ما مر وهذا بالإجماع وهذا متكرر مع قوله وهي أم ولد وأجيب بأن ذلك في ذات الأمة وهذا في الأولاد فلا وهي
Al-Muhit said: If he wrote a kitaba for his share without the permission of his partner, then she became pregnant from him, she is his umm walad and she is a mukatab as she was according to them (Sahibayn), because all of her became his umm walad, and he owns the share of his partner through guarantee because the kitaba does not split according to them, so he guarantees half of her value or half of her 'aqr to his partner and half of the 'aqr to her. And there is disagreement according to the statement of Imam: Some say that all does not become umm walad because istilad did not confer the right of freedom in the share of the one using istilad immediately, so he does not guarantee anything to his partner, and he guarantees all of the 'aqr to the mukatab. And some say that all becomes umm walad for him because istilad in his share operates immediately due to his ownership in it, so the one using istilad owns it, and he guarantees half of her value and half of the 'aqr to his partner, and half to the mukatab. And if the one who did not write kitaba had intercourse with her and she became pregnant from him, she is his umm walad, and the kitaba is valid, and he does not own the share of the mukatab through istilad according to him. And it was said: the kitaba should be dissolved by the mere act of istilad. And according to them (Sahibayn), he owns the share of his partner in the mukatab because all became a mukatab by the first kitaba and all became umm walad. And if he wrote a kitaba for her without his partner's permission, and she acquired wealth and paid and became free, then she acquired wealth, then the non-kitaba partner appeared, he has half of her earnings before payment of the price, and her earnings after payment belong to her. And according to them, it is valid. And if the second (co-owner) performed tadbir and did not have intercourse with her, then she became unable (tajuz), the tadbir is void and she is umm walad for the first, and he guarantees to his partner half of her value and half of her 'aqr, and the child belongs to the first. And if both wrote a kitaba for her, then one of them freed her while wealthy, and she became unable on the day she is free, the earnings are hers, and she takes half of what was paid from the mukatab. And if the mukatab gave birth to a daughter, and the daughter gave birth to a son, and one of them claimed istilad from him, then if the mukatab became unable, the daughter becomes umm walad for the one who had intercourse, and he guarantees to his partner half of her value because the child was conceived when her mother became unable, so the one using istilad owns her from the time of conception. If she did not become unable and the other partner freed the daughter after conception, it is valid and there is no khidmat (service) on her, and her child is free according to Imam. According to them, if the daughter pays, she becomes free, and there is no guarantee and no khidmat. If the daughter becomes unable, then the mother, the daughter is like an umm walad between two partners; one of them freed her. (Then follows multiple cases of joint ownership and inheritance.) The author said: (And any payment of 'aqr to the mukatab is valid) meaning any payment of 'aqr to the mukatab is permissible because it is her right while the kitaba stands; if she becomes unable, she returns it to the master. Al-Inaya said: meaning if he paid before her inability, and this is the statement of Imam. According to them, she becomes umm walad for the first and the entire dower is incumbent upon him because intercourse in the Abode of Islam is not free from either valid guarantee or deterrent penal measure; the penal measure is removed due to the legal doubt, so 'aqr becomes obligatory. If she becomes unable and is returned to slavery, she is returned to the master due to the apparent exclusivity of his ownership. And in al-Mabsut: A man wrote a kitaba for his slave woman, then died leaving two sons; one of them had istilad of her; she has an option: if she wishes, she may declare herself unable and become his umm walad, and he guarantees half of her value and half of her 'aqr to his partner; if she wishes, she may continue her kitaba and take her 'aqr, and the penal measure is dropped due to the legal doubt of ownership. The author said: (And if the second performed tadbir and did not have intercourse with her, then she became unable, the tadbir is void and she is umm walad for the first) and this is by consensus. According to them (Sahibayn), because the one who had istilad owned her before her inability; according to him (Imam), because with inability it becomes clear that all of her is umm walad for the first and that he had no ownership in her. Ownership is a condition for the validity of tadbir, unlike the establishment of lineage because apparent ownership is sufficient. For this reason, if one buys a slave woman and performs tadbir on her, then she is reclaimed, the tadbir is void; if he had istilad of her and she is reclaimed, it is not void and the child is free for a price. So here too, she is umm walad for the first because he owns the share of his partner and completes the istilad as possible. The author said: (And he guarantees to his partner half of her value) because he owns half of her through istilad as we explained before. The author said: (And half of her 'aqr) because he had intercourse with a joint slave woman belonging to both, so 'aqr is obligatory upon him proportionally, as we explained before. The author said: (And the child belongs to the first) because his claim was valid as previously mentioned, and this is by consensus. This is repeated with his statement 'and she is umm walad' and it is answered that that concerns the essence of the slave woman, while this concerns the offspring, so there is no repetition.
Source pages p. 104

Commentary
This passage continues the discussion of istilad on a joint mukatab, presenting additional scenarios from al-Muhit and the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq. The first scenario deals with a co-owner who writes a kitaba for his share without the other's permission: According to Sahibayn, the woman becomes full umm walad for him, and he owes compensation to his partner. According to Imam, there are two views: some say only his share is affected, others say the whole becomes umm walad. Another scenario: if the non-kitaba co-owner has intercourse and she becomes pregnant, she becomes his umm walad but the kitaba continues; however, he does not own the other's share. The passage then discusses the interaction of tadbir with istilad: if the second co-owner performs tadbir but does not have intercourse, and she becomes unable, the tadbir is void and the first co-owner's istilad prevails. Compensation rules are repeated: the first co-owner must pay half the value and half the 'aqr. Children born from the mukatab woman follow the mother's status. A long series of sub-cases (daughter giving birth, etc.) shows how the rulings apply in complex family situations. The matn then discusses the payment of 'aqr: according to Imam, payment to the mukatab is valid before her inability; according to Sahibayn, she becomes umm walad and the full 'aqr is due. A case from al-Mabsut shows that when a man dies leaving two sons, the mukatab woman has an option to complete her kitaba or become umm walad. The passage concludes by emphasizing that the child belongs to the first co-owner by consensus, and there is no repetition in the text because the earlier statement about the woman being umm walad is distinct from the ruling about the child.

Key Terms
عقر ('aqr): The dower or compensation payable for intercourse with a slave woman, especially in cases of legal doubt (shubha).
تجزؤ (tajazzi): The possibility of splitting; here, whether the kitaba contract can be split between the two co-owners' shares.
تدبير (tadbir): A declaration by a master that a slave will be free upon the master's death.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Sahibayn, what is the ruling if a co-owner writes a kitaba for his share of a joint slave woman without his partner's permission, and then has istilad?
A) The woman becomes full umm walad for him, and he must compensate his partner.
B) Only his share becomes umm walad; the other share remains mukatab.
C) The kitaba is void and the woman becomes free.
D) The woman remains a mukatab for both and the child is free.

Key Takeaway
In an intra-Hanafi dispute, the Sahibayn's ruling that istilad on a joint mukatab makes the whole woman umm walad, requiring full compensation, is the mufta bihi position.

Nikah — Marriage
advanced
10 min
Tadbir and Istilad on a Joint Mukatab: Priorities and Compensation
Matn and commentary on tadbir, 'aqr, and option in al-Mabsut

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to determine the interaction of tadbir and istilad on a joint mukatab and state the compensation obligations and the consensus on the child.

Core Idea
Tadbir is void when istilad later materializes; the first co-owner owns the child by consensus.

The passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq also addresses what happens when the second co-owner performs tadbir but does not have intercourse, and how istilad by the first co-owner overrides it. The compensation rules are consistently applied, and the child's parentage is resolved by consensus. Additionally, the payment of 'aqr and the option of the mukatab when a co-owner dies are discussed.

Guided Path
1
Understand the tadbir scenario
The second co-owner (who did not write kitaba) performs tadbir (declares the slave free upon his death) but does not have intercourse. Then the woman becomes unable (tajuz) to pay her kitaba. What happens to the tadbir and her status?
Tadbir requires ownership at the time of death; if she later becomes owned by the first co-owner, tadbir fails.
2
Why tadbir is void and she becomes umm walad
According to both Imam and Sahibayn, the tadbir is void and she becomes umm walad for the first co-owner. For Sahibayn, the first co-owner already owned her before her inability (since istilad gave full ownership). For Imam, the inability reveals that she was always umm walad for the first, meaning the second never had valid ownership for tadbir.
The principle: ownership is a condition for tadbir; if it was absent, tadbir is void ab initio.
3
Compensation rules reiterated
The first co-owner must guarantee half her value and half her 'aqr to his partner. This is the standard compensation for istilad on a joint slave.
The 'aqr is for the intercourse that caused istilad.
4
Consensus on the child
The child belongs to the first co-owner by consensus. The author notes that this is not a repetition: the earlier statement that she is umm walad refers to her own status, while this statement specifically affirms the child's lineage.
5
Examine the payment of 'aqr and the option in al-Mabsut
The matn states that any payment of 'aqr to the mukatab is valid. According to Imam, if paid before her inability, it is her right; if she becomes unable, she returns it to the master. According to Sahibayn, she becomes umm walad, so the full 'aqr is due. Al-Mabsut adds that when a man dies leaving two sons, the mukatab has an option: become umm walad and take compensation, or continue kitaba and take 'aqr.
The option shows the woman has a choice in how to proceed.

لأنه يملك نصفها بالاستيلاد على ما بينا قبل ذلك. قال رحمه الله : ( ونصف عقرها لأنه وطئ جارية مشتركة بينهما فيجب عليه العقر بحسابه وقد بيناه من قبل. قال رحمه الله : (والولد للأول) لأن دعواه قد صحت على ما مر وهذا بالإجماع وهذا متكرر مع قوله وهي أم ولد وأجيب بأن ذلك في ذات الأمة وهذا في الأولاد فلا وهي
Al-Muhit said: If he wrote a kitaba for his share without the permission of his partner, then she became pregnant from him, she is his umm walad and she is a mukatab as she was according to them (Sahibayn), because all of her became his umm walad, and he owns the share of his partner through guarantee because the kitaba does not split according to them, so he guarantees half of her value or half of her 'aqr to his partner and half of the 'aqr to her. And there is disagreement according to the statement of Imam: Some say that all does not become umm walad because istilad did not confer the right of freedom in the share of the one using istilad immediately, so he does not guarantee anything to his partner, and he guarantees all of the 'aqr to the mukatab. And some say that all becomes umm walad for him because istilad in his share operates immediately due to his ownership in it, so the one using istilad owns it, and he guarantees half of her value and half of the 'aqr to his partner, and half to the mukatab. And if the one who did not write kitaba had intercourse with her and she became pregnant from him, she is his umm walad, and the kitaba is valid, and he does not own the share of the mukatab through istilad according to him. And it was said: the kitaba should be dissolved by the mere act of istilad. And according to them (Sahibayn), he owns the share of his partner in the mukatab because all became a mukatab by the first kitaba and all became umm walad. And if he wrote a kitaba for her without his partner's permission, and she acquired wealth and paid and became free, then she acquired wealth, then the non-kitaba partner appeared, he has half of her earnings before payment of the price, and her earnings after payment belong to her. And according to them, it is valid. And if the second (co-owner) performed tadbir and did not have intercourse with her, then she became unable (tajuz), the tadbir is void and she is umm walad for the first, and he guarantees to his partner half of her value and half of her 'aqr, and the child belongs to the first. And if both wrote a kitaba for her, then one of them freed her while wealthy, and she became unable on the day she is free, the earnings are hers, and she takes half of what was paid from the mukatab. And if the mukatab gave birth to a daughter, and the daughter gave birth to a son, and one of them claimed istilad from him, then if the mukatab became unable, the daughter becomes umm walad for the one who had intercourse, and he guarantees to his partner half of her value because the child was conceived when her mother became unable, so the one using istilad owns her from the time of conception. If she did not become unable and the other partner freed the daughter after conception, it is valid and there is no khidmat (service) on her, and her child is free according to Imam. According to them, if the daughter pays, she becomes free, and there is no guarantee and no khidmat. If the daughter becomes unable, then the mother, the daughter is like an umm walad between two partners; one of them freed her. (Then follows multiple cases of joint ownership and inheritance.) The author said: (And any payment of 'aqr to the mukatab is valid) meaning any payment of 'aqr to the mukatab is permissible because it is her right while the kitaba stands; if she becomes unable, she returns it to the master. Al-Inaya said: meaning if he paid before her inability, and this is the statement of Imam. According to them, she becomes umm walad for the first and the entire dower is incumbent upon him because intercourse in the Abode of Islam is not free from either valid guarantee or deterrent penal measure; the penal measure is removed due to the legal doubt, so 'aqr becomes obligatory. If she becomes unable and is returned to slavery, she is returned to the master due to the apparent exclusivity of his ownership. And in al-Mabsut: A man wrote a kitaba for his slave woman, then died leaving two sons; one of them had istilad of her; she has an option: if she wishes, she may declare herself unable and become his umm walad, and he guarantees half of her value and half of her 'aqr to his partner; if she wishes, she may continue her kitaba and take her 'aqr, and the penal measure is dropped due to the legal doubt of ownership. The author said: (And if the second performed tadbir and did not have intercourse with her, then she became unable, the tadbir is void and she is umm walad for the first) and this is by consensus. According to them (Sahibayn), because the one who had istilad owned her before her inability; according to him (Imam), because with inability it becomes clear that all of her is umm walad for the first and that he had no ownership in her. Ownership is a condition for the validity of tadbir, unlike the establishment of lineage because apparent ownership is sufficient. For this reason, if one buys a slave woman and performs tadbir on her, then she is reclaimed, the tadbir is void; if he had istilad of her and she is reclaimed, it is not void and the child is free for a price. So here too, she is umm walad for the first because he owns the share of his partner and completes the istilad as possible. The author said: (And he guarantees to his partner half of her value) because he owns half of her through istilad as we explained before. The author said: (And half of her 'aqr) because he had intercourse with a joint slave woman belonging to both, so 'aqr is obligatory upon him proportionally, as we explained before. The author said: (And the child belongs to the first) because his claim was valid as previously mentioned, and this is by consensus. This is repeated with his statement 'and she is umm walad' and it is answered that that concerns the essence of the slave woman, while this concerns the offspring, so there is no repetition.
Source pages p. 104

Commentary
This passage continues the discussion of istilad on a joint mukatab, presenting additional scenarios from al-Muhit and the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq. The first scenario deals with a co-owner who writes a kitaba for his share without the other's permission: According to Sahibayn, the woman becomes full umm walad for him, and he owes compensation to his partner. According to Imam, there are two views: some say only his share is affected, others say the whole becomes umm walad. Another scenario: if the non-kitaba co-owner has intercourse and she becomes pregnant, she becomes his umm walad but the kitaba continues; however, he does not own the other's share. The passage then discusses the interaction of tadbir with istilad: if the second co-owner performs tadbir but does not have intercourse, and she becomes unable, the tadbir is void and the first co-owner's istilad prevails. Compensation rules are repeated: the first co-owner must pay half the value and half the 'aqr. Children born from the mukatab woman follow the mother's status. A long series of sub-cases (daughter giving birth, etc.) shows how the rulings apply in complex family situations. The matn then discusses the payment of 'aqr: according to Imam, payment to the mukatab is valid before her inability; according to Sahibayn, she becomes umm walad and the full 'aqr is due. A case from al-Mabsut shows that when a man dies leaving two sons, the mukatab woman has an option to complete her kitaba or become umm walad. The passage concludes by emphasizing that the child belongs to the first co-owner by consensus, and there is no repetition in the text because the earlier statement about the woman being umm walad is distinct from the ruling about the child.

Key Terms
عقر ('aqr): The dower or compensation payable for intercourse with a slave woman.
تدبير (tadbir): A declaration that a slave will be free upon the master's death.
تجزؤ (tajazzi): Splitting; here it is used in the context of kitaba not splitting.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the tadbir scenario, what is the consensus regarding the child born to the first co-owner?
A) The child is shared between the two co-owners.
B) The child belongs to the first co-owner.
C) The child is free and owes no compensation.
D) The child belongs to the second co-owner.

Key Takeaway
Tadbir by a second co-owner is void when the woman becomes unable and istilad by the first co-owner takes effect, with compensation standard and the child's lineage affirmed by consensus.

Ruling on the Mukatab's Inability and Rescission of Kitabah
States the ruling on ajz and faskh with proofs and intra-madhhab details

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a mukatab fails to pay an installment, explain the proof from the action of Umar (ra), and distinguish the correct narration regarding the slave's right to rescind.

Core Idea
A mukatab's inability to pay triggers rescission of kitabah and return to slavery, but only by judicial decree at the master's demand.

The kitabah contract is a special arrangement that allows a slave to earn freedom by paying installments. But what happens if the slave fails to pay? This lesson from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains the ruling on the mukatab's inability (ajz) and the rescission of the kitabah. We will examine the proof from the action of Caliph Umar (ra), the binding nature of the contract, and the judge's role in decreeing the return to slavery.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal issue
What happens when a mukatab fails to pay a due installment? The passage addresses this specific question and the consequences.
Focus on the term 'ajz (inability) as defined by failure to pay a najm (installment).
2
State the ruling
The kitabah is rescinded, the mukatab returns to the rulings of slavery, and any property in his hand goes to the master. However, this requires a judicial decree at the master's request.
Note that the rescission is not automatic; a judge must rule on the inability.
3
Analyze the proof
The ruling is supported by qiyas (analogy) and by the explicit action of Umar (ra), who rescinded the kitabah and returned the slave to slavery. This athar is treated as marfu' (raised to the Prophet).
Also note the silence of Ali (ra) does not negate the ruling.
4
Examine the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
There are two narrations: (1) kitabah is binding only on the master, so the slave can rescind without the master's consent; (2) it is binding on both, so the slave cannot rescind unilaterally. The first is the correct (mufta bihi) position.
The phrase 'or his master with his consent' indicates the master cannot unilaterally rescind without the slave's consent.
5
Consider procedural and exceptional cases
The judge's decree is obligatory (wajib) when the master demands. Special cases: multiple slaves under one kitabah, multiple masters, apostasy, and death of the master. These affect the rescission process.
Review the examples from al-Muhit cited in the passage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب المكاتب باب موت المكاتب وعجزه وموت المولى وفَسْخُهَا أَوْ سَيِّدُهُ بِرِضَاهُ وَعَادَ أَحْكَامُ الرِّقِّ وَمَا فِي يَدِهِ لِسَيِّدِهِ. يدرك بالقياس كالخبر ولأنه عقد إرفاق حتى كان التأجيل فيه سنة ولهما ما روي عن عمر رضي الله تعالى عنه فسخها بعجز المكاتب عن نجم ورده إلى الرق. والأثر فيه كالمرفوع. وما رواه عن علي : لا ينفي الفسخ إذا عجز عن نجم بل هو سكوت عنه . وأفاد بقوله «أو سيده برضاه» أن الكتابة لازمة من جانب المولى غير لازمة من جانب العبد ، فلو أراد العبد أن يفسخ الكتابة وأبى المولى ذلك فللعبد ذلك في الرواية الصحيحة، والرواية الثانية أنها لازمة من جانب العبد أيضاً فليس له أن يفسخها بغير رضا المولى. والمراد بقوله «فسخها» يعني الحاكم يحكم بعجزه لأنه واجب عند طلب المولى وله ولاية ذلك وإن لم يرض العبد فلا بد من القضاء كالرد بالعيب. وظاهر قوله مكاتب عجز عن نجم صادق بما إذا كاتبه وحده أو مع غيره وليس كذلك بل هو خاص بما إذا كاتبه وحده قال في المحيط : ولو كاتب عبدين كتابة واحدة فعجز أحدهما فرده القاضي في الرق والقاضي لا يعلم بمكاتبة الآخر ثم أدى الآخر الكتابة عتقا جميعاً لأنه لم يصح رد الأول في الرق ما دام الآخر قادراً على أداء بدل الكتابة، ولهذا لو علم القاضي بكتابة الآخر لا يرد حتى يجتمعا، ولو كاتب الموليان عبداً لهما كتابة واحدة فعجز لم يرد في الرق حتى يجتمع الموليان لأنه إذا غاب أحدهما كان الفسخ في نصيب الآخر متعذراً، ولو مات المولى عن ورثة فلبعضهم الرد في الرق بقضاء وليس له ذلك بغير قضاء لأن بعض الورثة ينتصب خصماً عن الميت فيما له وفيما عليه. وفي المحيط : كاتب عبديه كتابة واحدة فارتد أحدهما ولحق بدار الحرب فعجز الحاضر لم يرده القاضي في الرق وإن رده لم يكن رداً للآخر حتى لو رجع مسلماً لم يرد إلى مولاه، فلو قال «في كتابة واحدة» لكان أولى اهـ . قال رحمه الله : (وعاد أحكام الرق) يعني إذا عجز عاد إلى أحكام الرق لأن الكتابة قد انفسخت وفك الحجر كان لأجل عقد الكتابة فلا يبقى بدون العقد، ولا يخفى أن المؤلف قال وعاد أحكام الرق ولم يقل عاد إلى الرق لأنه فيه باق. قال رحمه الله : (وما في يده لسيده) لأنه ظهر أنه كسب عبده إذا كان موقوفاً عليه أو على المولى على تقدير الأداء كان له وعلى تقدير العجز كان للمولى وقد تحقق العجز فكان لمولاه.
Book of the Mukatab: Chapter on the Death of the Mukatab, His Inability, and the Death of the Master, and Its Rescission by the Master with His Consent, and the Return of the Rulings of Slavery, and What is in His Hand Goes to His Master. It is understood by analogy like the narration, because it is a contract of kindness so that its deferment was one year, and for them (the two companions) what was narrated from Umar (may Allah be pleased with him): he rescinded it due to the mukatab's inability to pay a installment and returned him to slavery. The athar is like a marfu' hadith. And what was narrated from Ali does not negate rescission when unable to pay a installment, rather it is silence about it. And his statement 'or his master with his consent' indicates that the kitabah is binding on the master's side but not binding on the slave's side. If the slave wants to rescind the kitabah and the master refuses, the slave has that right in the correct narration; the second narration says it is binding on the slave's side as well, so he cannot rescind it without the master's consent. And by his statement 'its rescission' is meant the judge rules his inability because it is obligatory when the master demands, and he has authority over that even if the slave does not consent, so judicial decree is necessary like the return due to defect. And the apparent meaning of his statement 'a mukatab unable to pay a installment' applies whether he contracted individually or with others, but it is not so; rather it is specific to when he contracted individually. Al-Muhit said: If someone made a single kitabah contract with two slaves and one becomes unable and the judge returns him to slavery while the judge does not know about the other's contract, then the other pays the kitabah price, both become free because the first's return to slavery is not valid as long as the other is capable of paying the kitabah price. Hence if the judge knew of the other's kitabah, he would not return him until they are both together. If two masters made a single kitabah contract with one slave and he becomes unable, he is not returned to slavery until both masters agree because if one is absent, rescission in the other's share is impossible. If the master dies leaving heirs, some of them may return him to slavery by judicial decree, but not without it because some heirs represent the deceased in what is for him and against him. In al-Muhit: If someone made a single kitabah contract with two slaves, one apostatized and joined the land of war, and the present one became unable, the judge does not return him to slavery; even if he returned him, it would not be a return for the other, so that if he returns as a Muslim, he is not returned to his master. So if he had said 'in a single kitabah' it would be better. End. He said (may Allah have mercy on him): (And the rulings of slavery return) meaning if he becomes unable, he returns to the rulings of slavery because the kitabah is rescinded and the lifting of interdiction was due to the kitabah contract, so it does not remain without the contract. It is not hidden that the author said 'the rulings of slavery return' and did not say 'he returns to slavery' because he is still in it. He said (may Allah have mercy on him): (And what is in his hand goes to his master) because it becomes clear that it is his slave's earning, and if it was suspended for him or for the master on condition of payment, it would be for him, and on condition of inability it would be for the master, and inability has occurred so it goes to his master.
Source pages p. 108

Commentary
This passage is a sharh (expansion) on the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq regarding the mukatab's inability (ajz) and the rescission (faskh) of the kitabah contract. The author first states the core ruling: if the mukatab becomes unable to pay a installment, the kitabah is rescinded, he returns to the rulings of slavery, and any wealth or property in his possession reverts to his master. The matn also mentions that the master may rescind the contract by his own consent (i.e., voluntarily giving up the kitabah). The commentary then provides proofs: it is reached by qiyas (analogy) and by the narration from Umar (ra), who rescinded the contract when a mukatab failed to pay and returned him to slavery. This athar is treated as having the authority of a marfu' hadith because it is a practice of the Rightly Guided Caliph. The commentator notes that the narration from Ali (ra) does not deny such rescission but is merely silent. He then clarifies an important point: the kitabah contract is binding (lazim) on the master but not on the slave. This is derived from the phrase 'or his master with his consent'—the master cannot unilaterally rescind, but the slave can, in the correct narration (riwayah sahihah). Another narration holds it binding on both sides. The commentary then explains that the 'rescission' referred to in the matn actually means the judge's declaration of the mukatab's inability, as the judge has jurisdiction even without the slave's consent. The author then addresses a subtlety: the rule applies specifically when the mukatab contracted individually, not when two slaves are under one kitabah contract. He cites lengthy passages from al-Muhit to illustrate cases involving multiple slaves or multiple masters, apostasy, and death of the master. The key principle: the return to the rulings of slavery means he is subject to all legal consequences of slavery (e.g., no right to contract, his earnings belong to the master) because the kitabah has been rescinded and the temporary lifting of interdiction (fakk al-hajr) ceases. The author ends by explaining that the master takes what the mukatab had in hand because it becomes clear that it was the slave's earning, and since inability actualized, it belongs to the master.

Key Terms
مكاتب (mukātab): A slave who has entered into a kitabah contract with his master, whereby he pays a sum in installments and becomes free upon completion.
كتابة (kitābah): A contract between master and slave where the slave pays a fixed amount over time in exchange for freedom.
عجز (ʿajz): Inability of the mukatab to pay a due installment (najm) when due.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a mukatab fails to pay an installment, what is the status of his kitabah contract according to the Hanafi school?
A) The kitabah is automatically rescinded without any action.
B) The kitabah remains valid and the missed installment is added to the end.
C) The kitabah is rescinded by judicial decree when the master demands it, and the mukatab returns to slavery.
D) The mukatab is given an extension but the contract continues.

Key Takeaway
A mukatab's inability to pay a installment leads to rescission of kitabah and return to slavery, but only through a judge's decree at the master's demand.

The Kitabah Survives the Mukatab's Death: The Hanafi Position
Presents the dispute and Hanafi proof with istinad.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the death of a mukatab with wealth, explain the Hanafi proof using istinad, and compare it with the Shafi'i position.

Core Idea
The kitabah is a contract of exchange, so the mukatab's death does not void it; his freedom is retroactively established upon payment from his estate.

When a mukatab (slave under a kitabah contract) dies with sufficient wealth to pay the outstanding price, what happens to the contract? The Hanafi school, following Ibn Mas'ud, holds that the contract remains valid and is fulfilled from his estate. This lesson unpacks the Hanafi reasoning, including the key principle of istinad (retroactive attribution), and contrasts it with the Shafi'i position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed scenario
What exactly is the ruling in question? (Mukatab dies with wealth, is kitabah rescinded?)
2
State the two competing views
Hanafi: not rescinded; Shafi'i: rescinded. Note the supporting Sahaba.
3
Analyze the Hanafi proof
Why is kitabah like a sale? How does the principle of istinad apply? Use the hunting analogy.
4
Examine the Shafi'i proof
Why does freedom require a living person? How does the contract become impossible?
5
Evaluate the thamarah
What practical difference does this make for the mukatab's children and estate?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (وإن مات وله مال لم تفسخ) وهذا قول ابن مسعود وبه أخذ علماؤنا . وقال زيد بن ثابت تنفسخ الكتابة بموته وبه أخذ الإمام الشافعي له أن العقد لو بقي لبقي لتحصيل العتق بالأداء وقد تعذر إثباته ،فبطل، وهذا لأن العتق لا يخلوا إما أن يثبت العتق قبل الموت أو بعده مقتصراً أو مستنداً لا وجه إلى الأول لعدم شرطه وهو الأداء والشيء لا يسبق شرطه، ولا إلى الثاني لأن الميت ليس بمحل لنزول العتق عليه لأن العتق إثبات قوة الميت يتصور في المالكية بخلاف ما إذا مات المولى لأنه ليس بمعقود عليه بل عاقد والعقد يبطل بموت المعقود عليه لا بموت العاقد، ولأن المولى يصلح أن يكون معتقاً بعد الموت كما هو. تفسخ وتؤدي كتابته من ماله وحكم بعتقه في آخر حياته وإن ترك ولداً ولد في كتابته إذا قال أنت حر بعد موتي. ولنا أن الكتابة عقد معاوضة لا تنفسخ بموت أحد المتعاقدين وهو المولى فلا ينفسخ بموت الآخر وهو العبد كالبيع ولأن قضية المعاوضة المساواة فإذا بقي العقد بعد موت المولى لحاجته إلى الولاء وغيره جاز أن يبقى بعد موت العبد لحاجته إلى الحرية ليتوصل إلى حرية أولاده، ولو مات عاجزاً تفسخ الكتابة، ولو قذفه إنسان بعد الأداء يلزمه الحد، وقيل الأداء لا يلزمه الحد لأن العتق ثبت مستنداً إلى آخر جزء من أجزاء حياته فلا يظهر الاستناد في حق هذا الحكم. قال رحمه الله : (وتؤدي كتابته من ماله) يعني يؤدي من خلفه فيكون أداء الخليفة كأدائه بنفسه. فإن قيل : الأداء فعل والاستناد يكون في أحكام الشريعة قلنا : نعم لكن فعل الثابت مضافاً إلى حسي الثبوت وهذه الإضافة شرعية ألا ترى أن من رمى صيداً فمات قبل أن يصيبه ثم أصابه صار مالكاً له حتى يورث عنه والمالك ليس بأهل لكن لما صح السبب والملك يثبت بعد تمام السبب وتمامه بالإضافة إليه وهو ليس أهلاً له ثبت الملك من حين الإمكان وهو آخر جزء من أجزاء حياته فكذا هنا. وفي الأصل: إذا مات المكاتب عن وفاء وعليه ديون لأجنبي سوى بدل الكتابة وله مال يوفي وله وصايا يبدأ من تركته بدين الأجنبي ثم بدل الكتابة وتبطل وصاياه وما بقي يقسم بين ورثته، وإن لم يبق بعد قضاء الدين شيء يبدأ ببدل الكتابة ولا يبدأ بالدين، وإن لم يترك مالاً إلا ديناً على الناس فاستسعى المولود في الكتابة فعجز يرد في الرق فإذا خرج الدين بعد ذلك فذلك للمولى ا هـ . قال رحمه الله : (وحكم بعتقه في آخر حياته) بأن يقام الترك الموجود منه في آخر حياته مقام التخلية بين المال والمولى وهو الأداء المستحق عليه وما بقي فهو لورثته. قال في نوادر بشر عن الثاني : مات مكاتب عن وفاء وله أولاد أمته فمات بعض قبل الأداء فأدى ما عليه وبقي مال فهو ميراث ولا يرث الابن الميت وما تركه الابن الميت فهو لأمه وإخوته، ولو كان الولد معه في عقد الكتابة ثم مات بعد أبيه ثم أديت الكتابة لم يرث أباه . وفي نواد ابن سماعة محمد مكاتب مات وترك ابناً ولد له في الكتابة وترك ألفي درهم ديناً على الناس فاكتسب ألف درهم وأداها في كتابة أبيه ثم خرج دين الأب وله أخ فإن الألفين ميراث بينهما ولا يرجع الابن بما أدى في الألفين، وإن لم يؤد الابن ذلك من ماله فله أن يأخذ من مال الأب. وفي المنتقى : مكاتب مات وله دين على الناس وله مولود في الكتابة يسعى في الكتابة على نجومها وله ابنان حران أيضاً ثم مات أحد الابنين الحرين ثم خرج ما للمكاتب على الناس فأديت من ذلك بدل الكتابة فالفاضل بين الولد الحر والمولود في الكتابة ويرث الابن الحر أخاه الذي مات بعد موت الأب والابن المولود في الكتابة لا يرث من أخيه الذي مات بعد موت الأب وفي التتارخانية : مات الرجل عن مكاتبه وله ورثه ذكور وأناث ثم مات المكاتب عن وفاء يؤدي من ذلك بدل الكتابة ويكون بين الورثة الذكور والإناث.
He said (may Allah have mercy on him): (And if he dies and has wealth, it is not rescinded) — this is the saying of Ibn Mas'ud, and our scholars adopted it. Zayd ibn Thabit said: The kitabah is rescinded by his death, and Imam al-Shafi'i adopted this. His proof: if the contract remained, it would remain for the acquisition of freedom through payment, but its realization is impossible, so it is void. This is because freedom must either be established before death or after death as a restricted or retroactive effect. The first is impossible because its condition (payment) is absent, and a thing cannot precede its condition. The second is also impossible because the dead is not a locus for the descent of freedom — freedom is the establishment of strength, which can be imagined in the living, unlike the case of the master's death because he is not the contracted subject but the contractor, and the contract is voided by the death of the contracted subject, not the contractor. And because the master is fit to be an emancipator after death as well. It is rescinded, and his kitabah is paid from his wealth, and a ruling is made for his freedom at the last moment of his life, even if he left a child born during his kitabah and he had said 'you are free after my death'. Our proof: the kitabah is a contract of exchange (mu'awadah) that is not rescinded by the death of one of the two contractors — the master — so it is not rescinded by the death of the other — the slave — like a sale. And because the nature of exchange is equivalence; if the contract remains after the master's death due to the need for wala' and other things, it is permissible for it to remain after the slave's death due to the need for freedom to facilitate the freedom of his children. If he dies unable, the kitabah is rescinded. If someone accuses him of fornication after payment, the prescribed hadd (80 lashes) is obligatory upon the accuser; and some said payment does not require the hadd because the freedom is established retroactively to the last part of his life, so the retroactivity does not appear regarding this ruling. He said (may Allah have mercy on him): (And his kitabah is paid from his wealth) meaning his successor pays, so the payment of the successor is like his own payment. If it is said: payment is an act, and retroactivity applies in shariah rulings, we say: yes, but the act of the one established is attributed to sensory existence, and this attribution is shariah-based. Do you not see that if someone shoots at game and dies before it hits, then it hits, he becomes its owner so that it is inherited from him — even though the owner is not eligible (for ownership) — but because the cause is sound, and ownership is established after the completion of the cause and its completion is attributed to him, and he is not eligible for it, ownership is established from the time of possibility, which is the last part of his life. So here similarly. In al-Asl: if a mukatab dies with sufficient wealth and owes debts to outsiders besides the kitabah price, and has wealth to pay, and has bequests, then his estate begins with the outsider's debt, then the kitabah price, and his bequests are void; what remains is divided among his heirs. If nothing remains after paying the debt, he begins with the kitabah price and does not begin with the debt. If he leaves no wealth except a debt owed by people, then the child (born during kitabah) works to pay the kitabah installments, and if unable, he is returned to slavery; if the debt is collected afterward, it goes to the master. End. He said (may Allah have mercy on him): (And a ruling is made for his freedom at the last moment of his life) meaning the wealth left by him at the last moment of his life is considered as handing over the wealth to the master, i.e., the payment due from him, and what remains is for his heirs. He said in Nawadir Bishr from the second: a mukatab died with sufficient wealth and had children from his slave-wife; some died before payment; he paid what was due and wealth remained; it is inheritance, and the deceased son does not inherit, and what the deceased son left is for his mother and siblings. If the child was included in the same kitabah contract and then died after his father, and then the kitabah was paid, he does not inherit from his father. In Nawadir Ibn Sam'ah: Muhammad said: a mukatab died leaving a son born during his kitabah and leaving 2000 dirhams as a debt owed by people; the son earned 1000 dirhams and paid it for his father's kitabah; then the father's debt was collected and he has a (free) brother; then the 2000 are inheritance between them, and the son does not take back what he paid from the 2000. If the son did not pay that from his own wealth, he may take from the father's wealth. In al-Muntaqa: a mukatab died, owed debt to people, and had a child born during his kitabah who works to pay the kitabah installments, and he also has two free sons; then one of the free sons died; then the mukatab's debt owed by people was collected, and from it the kitabah price was paid; the surplus is between the free son and the child born during kitabah; the free son inherits from his brother who died after the father's death, but the child born during kitabah does not inherit from that brother. In al-Tatar Khaniyyah: a man died leaving a mukatab, and his heirs are males and females; then the mukatab died with sufficient wealth; the kitabah price is paid from that and distributed among the male and female heirs.
Source pages p. 108

Commentary
This section presents a significant inter-madhhab dispute regarding the fate of a mukatab who dies with sufficient wealth to pay the kitabah price. The Hanafi position, attributed to Ibn Mas'ud (ra), is that the kitabah is NOT rescinded by his death; rather, the kitabah price is paid from his estate, and he is considered to have become free at the last moment of his life. This allows his children born during the kitabah to become free as well. The opposing position, attributed to Zayd ibn Thabit (ra) and adopted by Imam al-Shafi'i, holds that the kitabah is rescinded upon the mukatab's death, and his estate goes to his heirs as a free man's estate (i.e., no kitabah price is due) or returns to the master. The Hanafi proof (dalil) is that the kitabah is a contract of exchange (mu'awadah) like a sale — it is not voided by the death of either party. The master's death does not void it because the contract is on the slave, not the master; similarly, the slave's death should not void it. The master can still receive the payment from the estate, and the slave's freedom is established retroactively upon payment. To address the objection that a dead person cannot be emancipated, the Hanafis use the principle of istinad (retroactive attribution) drawing an analogy with hunting: a hunter who shoots and dies before the arrow hits can still become the owner of the game at the moment of impact because the cause was sound; similarly, the payment by the estate is attributed to the mukatab's life. The commentary then provides detailed furu' (branches) from al-Asl, al-Nawadir, al-Muntaqa, and al-Tatar Khaniyyah about how the estate is distributed, priority of debts, and inheritance shares for children born during kitabah versus free children. Key points: (1) Outsider debts take priority over the kitabah price; (2) Bequests are void if the estate is insufficient; (3) Children born during kitabah who work to pay the price and become unable are returned to slavery; (4) Complex inheritance cases show that a child born during kitabah inherits from the father only if the kitabah is paid, but does not inherit from a free half-brother who died after the father.

Key Terms
استناد (istinād): Retroactive attribution of a legal effect to a prior moment in time, used here to establish the mukatab's freedom at the last moment of his life upon payment from his estate.
ولاء (walāʾ): Patronage bond between the emancipator and the freed slave, which remains with the master's heirs after the master's death.
معاوضة (muʿāwaḍah): Contract of exchange where each party gives something in return for something else, like sale; kitabah is considered such despite its kindness aspect.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the key Hanafi proof that the kitabah is not rescinded by the mukatab's death?
A) The kitabah is a contract of exchange (mu'awadah) like a sale, which survives death.
B) The master's consent is required for rescission.
C) The mukatab's children must be free.
D) The Prophet (SAW) explicitly stated so.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that the kitabah contract survives the mukatab's death; his estate pays the price, and he is deemed free retroactively.
